</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charitable_status">Charitable status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Charitable status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the UK Amnesty International has two principal arms, Amnesty International UK and Amnesty International Charity Ltd. Both are UK-based organizations but only the latter is a charity.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Principles">Principles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Principles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The core principle of Amnesty International is a focus on <a href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_conscience" class="mw-redirect" title="Prisoners of conscience">prisoners of conscience</a>, those persons imprisoned or prevented from expressing an opinion by means of violence. Along with this commitment to opposing repression of freedom of expression, Amnesty International's founding principles included non-intervention on political questions, a robust commitment to gathering facts about the various cases and promoting human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One key issue in the principles is in regards to those individuals who may advocate or tacitly support resorting to violence in struggles against repression. AI does not judge whether recourse to violence is justified or not. However, AI does not oppose the political use of violence in itself since <a href="/wiki/The_Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="The Universal Declaration of Human Rights">The Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>, in its preamble, foresees situations in which people could "be compelled to have recourse, as a last resort, to rebellion against tyranny and oppression". If a prisoner is serving a sentence imposed, after a fair trial, for activities involving violence, AI will not ask the government to release the prisoner.
</p><p>AI neither supports nor condemns the resort to violence by political opposition groups in itself, just as AI neither supports nor condemns a government policy of using military force in fighting against armed opposition movements. However, AI supports minimum humane standards that should be respected by governments and armed opposition groups alike. When an opposition group tortures or kills its captives, takes hostages, or commits deliberate and arbitrary killings, AI condemns these abuses.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (July 2011)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Amnesty_International#Dubious" title="Talk:Amnesty International">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Amnesty International opposes capital punishment in all cases, regardless of the crime committed, the circumstances surrounding the individual or the method of execution.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Objectives">Objectives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Objectives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Amnesty+International%22">"Amnesty International"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Amnesty+International%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Amnesty+International%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Amnesty+International%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Amnesty+International%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Amnesty+International%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:30%;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">Amnesty International's vision is of a world in which every person enjoys all of the human rights enshrined in the Universal Declaration of Human Rights and other international human rights standards.
In pursuit of this vision, Amnesty International's mission is to undertake research and action focused on preventing and ending grave abuses of the rights to physical and mental integrity, freedom of conscience and expression, and freedom from discrimination, within the context of its work to promote all human rights.</div>
<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">-Statute of Amnesty International, 27th International Council meeting, 2005</cite>
</p>
</div><p> Amnesty International primarily targets governments, but also reports on non-governmental bodies and private individuals ("<a href="/wiki/Non-state_actors" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-state actors">non-state actors</a>").
</p><p>There are six key areas which Amnesty deals with:<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women&#39;s rights">Women's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_rights" title="Children&#39;s rights">children's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minority_rights" title="Minority rights">minorities'</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_rights" title="Indigenous rights">indigenous rights</a></li>
<li>Ending <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a></li>
<li>Abolition of the death penalty</li>
<li>Rights of <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a></li>
<li>Rights of <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_conscience" title="Prisoner of conscience">prisoners of conscience</a></li>
<li>Protection of <a href="/wiki/Human_dignity" class="mw-redirect" title="Human dignity">human dignity</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Some specific aims are to: abolish the <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" class="mw-redirect" title="Death penalty">death penalty</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> end <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_punishment" title="Extrajudicial punishment">extra judicial executions</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">disappearances</a>", ensure prison conditions meet international human rights standards, ensure prompt and fair trial for all <a href="/wiki/Political_prisoner" title="Political prisoner">political prisoners</a>, ensure free education to all children worldwide, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.amnesty.org/en/what-we-do/sexual-and-reproductive-rights/abortion-facts">decriminalize abortion</a>, fight <a href="/wiki/Impunity" title="Impunity">impunity</a> from systems of justice, end the recruitment and use of <a href="/wiki/Military_use_of_children" class="mw-redirect" title="Military use of children">child soldiers</a>, free all <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_conscience" title="Prisoner of conscience">prisoners of conscience</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.amnesty.org/en/what-we-do/living-in-dignity">promote economic, social and cultural rights</a> for marginalized communities, protect <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_defender" title="Human rights defender">human rights defenders</a>, promote <a href="/wiki/Religious_tolerance" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious tolerance">religious tolerance</a>, protect <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBT rights">LGBT rights</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.amnesty.org/en/what-we-do/torture">stop torture and ill-treatment</a>, stop <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.amnesty.org/en/what-we-do/armed-conflict">unlawful killings in armed conflict</a>, uphold the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.amnesty.org/en/what-we-do/refugees-asylum-seekers-and-migrants">rights of refugees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">migrants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Asylum_seeker" title="Asylum seeker">asylum seekers</a>, and protect human dignity. It also supports worldwide <a href="/wiki/Decriminalizing_sex_work" title="Decriminalizing sex work">decriminalisation of prostitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AmInt2009MarchaGayDF.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/AmInt2009MarchaGayDF.JPG/220px-AmInt2009MarchaGayDF.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/AmInt2009MarchaGayDF.JPG/330px-AmInt2009MarchaGayDF.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/AmInt2009MarchaGayDF.JPG/440px-AmInt2009MarchaGayDF.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AmInt2009MarchaGayDF.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amnesty International at the 2009 Marcha Gay in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, 20 June 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Additionally, Amnesty International has developed ways to publicize information and mobilize public opinion. The organization considers the publication of impartial and accurate reports as one of its strengths. Reports are researched by: interviewing victims and officials, observing trials, working with local human rights activists, and monitoring the media. It aims to issue timely press releases and publishes information in newsletters and on web sites. It also sends official missions to countries to make courteous but insistent inquiries. 
</p><p>Campaigns to mobilize public opinion can take the form of individual, country, or thematic campaigns. Many techniques are deployed, such as direct appeals (for example, letter writing), media and publicity work, and public demonstrations. Often, fund-raising is integrated with campaigning. In 2018, the organization started to adopt a new communications strategy based on <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.campaignlive.co.uk/article/amnesty-international-wants-make-human-rights-popular/1592146">a message of shared humanity and a hope-based communications approach</a>.
</p><p>In situations which require immediate attention, Amnesty International calls on existing urgent action networks or crisis response networks; for all other matters, it calls on its membership. It considers the large size of its human resources to be another of its key strengths.
</p><p>The role of Amnesty International has a significant impact on getting citizens on board with focusing on human rights issues. These groups influence countries and governments to give their people justice with pressure and in human resources. An example of Amnesty International's work is writing letters to free imprisoned people that were put there for non-violent expressions. The group now has power, attends sessions, and became a source of information for the UN. The increase in participation of non-governmental organizations changes how we live today. <a href="/wiki/Felix_Dodds" title="Felix Dodds">Felix Dodds</a> states in a recent document: "In 1972 there were 39 democratic countries in the world; by 2002, there were 139."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> This shows that non-governmental organizations make enormous leaps within a short period of time for human rights.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Country_focus">Country focus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Country focus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HRM_TLV_091211_212.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/HRM_TLV_091211_212.jpg/220px-HRM_TLV_091211_212.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/HRM_TLV_091211_212.jpg/330px-HRM_TLV_091211_212.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/HRM_TLV_091211_212.jpg/440px-HRM_TLV_091211_212.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HRM_TLV_091211_212.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protesting <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>'s policy against <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_from_Africa_to_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Illegal immigration from Africa to Israel">African refugees</a>, Tel Aviv, 9 December 2011</div></div></div>
<p>Amnesty reports disproportionately on relatively more democratic and open countries,<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty.org_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty.org-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> arguing that its intention is not to produce a range of reports which statistically represents the world's human rights abuses, but rather to apply the pressure of public opinion to encourage improvements.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Demonstration_effect" title="Demonstration effect">demonstration effect</a> of the behaviour of both key Western governments and major non-Western states is an important factor: as one former Amnesty Secretary-General pointed out, "for many countries and a large number of people, the United States is a model," and according to one Amnesty manager, "large countries influence small countries."<sup id="cite_ref-ISQ05_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISQ05-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In addition, with the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, Amnesty felt that a greater emphasis on human rights in the North was needed to improve its credibility with its Southern critics by demonstrating its willingness to report on human rights issues in a truly global manner.<sup id="cite_ref-ISQ05_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISQ05-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to one academic study, as a result of these considerations the frequency of Amnesty's reports is influenced by a number of factors, besides the frequency and severity of human rights abuses. For example, Amnesty reports significantly more (than predicted by human rights abuses) on more economically powerful states; and on countries which receive US military aid, on the basis that this Western complicity in abuses increases the likelihood of public pressure being able to make a difference.<sup id="cite_ref-ISQ05_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISQ05-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In addition, around 1993–94, Amnesty consciously developed its media relations, producing fewer background reports and more press releases, to increase the impact of its reports. Press releases are partly driven by news coverage, to use existing news coverage as leverage to discuss Amnesty's human rights concerns. This increases Amnesty's focus on the countries the media is more interested in.<sup id="cite_ref-ISQ05_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISQ05-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Kristyan_Benedict" title="Kristyan Benedict">Kristyan Benedict</a>, Amnesty UK's campaign manager whose main focus is Syria, listed several countries as "regimes who abuse peoples' basic universal rights": <a href="/wiki/Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma">Burma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>. Benedict was criticized for including Israel in this short list on the basis that his opinion was garnered solely from "his own visits", with no other objective sources.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peretz_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peretz-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Amnesty's country focus is similar to that of some other comparable NGOs, notably <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>: between 1991 and 2000, Amnesty and HRW shared eight of ten countries in their "top ten" (by Amnesty press releases; 7 for Amnesty reports).<sup id="cite_ref-ISQ05_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISQ05-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In addition, six of the 10 countries most reported on by Human Rights Watch in the 1990s also made <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>'s and <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i>'s "most covered" lists during that time.<sup id="cite_ref-ISQ05_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISQ05-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding">Funding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Funding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Amnesty International is financed largely by fees and donations from its worldwide membership. It says that it does not accept donations from governments or governmental organizations. According to the AI website,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote><p>"these personal and unaffiliated donations allow AI to maintain full independence from any and all governments, political ideologies, economic interests or religions. We neither seek nor accept any funds for human rights research from governments or political parties and we accept support only from businesses that have been carefully vetted. By way of ethical fundraising leading to donations from individuals, we are able to stand firm and unwavering in our defence of universal and indivisible human rights."</p></blockquote>
<p>However, AI has received grants over the past ten years from the UK <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">Department for International Development</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_States_State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="United States State Department">United States State Department</a><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> and other governments.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>AI (USA) has received funding from the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Foundation" title="Rockefeller Foundation">Rockefeller Foundation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> but these funds are only used "in support of its human rights education work."<sup id="cite_ref-auto_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_and_controversies">Criticism and controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Criticism and controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Amnesty_International" title="Criticism of Amnesty International">Criticism of Amnesty International</a></div>
<p>Criticism of Amnesty International includes claims of excessive pay for management, underprotection of overseas staff, associating with organizations with a dubious record on human rights protection, <a href="/wiki/Selection_bias" title="Selection bias">selection bias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ideology" title="Ideology">ideological</a> and foreign policy bias against either non-<a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> countries<sup id="cite_ref-CAQ_FBoyle_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAQ_FBoyle-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a>-supported countries, or bias for <a href="/wiki/Terrorist_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrorist groups">terrorist groups</a>,.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>    A recent report also shows an internal toxic work environment.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The report of Amnesty condemned that after <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a> succeeded <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of China">General Secretary of the Communist Party of China</a> in 2012, human rights in China have become worse.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Amnesty International supports women's human right to access abortion services as basic healthcare, and the Vatican has levied criticism on Amnesty International for this.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Governments and their supporters have criticized Amnesty's criticism of their policies, including those of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Peretz_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peretz-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> for what they assert is one-sided reporting or a failure to treat threats to security as a mitigating factor. The actions of these governments, and of other governments critical of Amnesty International, have been the subject of human rights concerns voiced by Amnesty.
</p><p>The <i>Sudan Vision Daily</i>, a daily newspaper in <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, compared Amnesty to the US <a href="/wiki/National_Endowment_for_Democracy" title="National Endowment for Democracy">National Endowment for Democracy</a>, and claimed "it is, in essence, a <a href="/wiki/British_intelligence" class="mw-redirect" title="British intelligence">British intelligence</a> organization which is a part of the Government decision making system."<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CAGE_controversy">CAGE controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: CAGE controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Amnesty International suspended <a href="/wiki/Gita_Sahgal" title="Gita Sahgal">Gita Sahgal</a>, its gender unit head, after she criticized Amnesty in February 2010 for its high-profile associations with <a href="/wiki/Moazzam_Begg" title="Moazzam Begg">Moazzam Begg</a>, the director of <a href="/wiki/Cageprisoners" class="mw-redirect" title="Cageprisoners">Cageprisoners</a>, representing men in extrajudicial detention.<sup id="cite_ref-kerbaj_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kerbaj-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>"To be appearing on platforms with Britain's most famous supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a>, Begg, whom we treat as a human rights defender, is a gross error of judgment," she said.<sup id="cite_ref-kerbaj_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kerbaj-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aar_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aar-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Sahgal argued that by associating with Begg and Cageprisoners, Amnesty was risking its reputation on human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-kerbaj_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kerbaj-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> "As a former Guantanamo detainee, it was legitimate to hear his experiences, but as a supporter of the Taliban it was absolutely wrong to legitimise him as a partner," Sahgal said.<sup id="cite_ref-kerbaj_133-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kerbaj-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> She said she repeatedly brought the matter up with Amnesty for two years, to no avail.<sup id="cite_ref-dd_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dd-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> A few hours after the article was published, Sahgal was suspended from her position.<sup id="cite_ref-sigstate_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sigstate-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Amnesty's Senior Director of Law and Policy, Widney Brown, later said Sahgal raised concerns about Begg and Cageprisoners to her personally for the first time a few days before sharing them with the <i>Sunday Times</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-dd_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dd-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sahgal issued a statement saying she felt that Amnesty was risking its reputation by associating with and thereby politically legitimizing Begg, because Cageprisoners "actively promotes Islamic Right ideas and individuals".<sup id="cite_ref-sigstate_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sigstate-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> She said the issue was not about Begg's "freedom of opinion, nor about his right to propound his views: he already exercises these rights fully as he should. The issue is ... the importance of the human rights movement maintaining an objective distance from groups and ideas that are committed to systematic discrimination and fundamentally undermine the universality of human rights."<sup id="cite_ref-sigstate_140-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sigstate-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The controversy prompted responses by politicians, the writer <a href="/wiki/Salman_Rushdie" title="Salman Rushdie">Salman Rushdie</a>, and journalist <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Hitchens" title="Christopher Hitchens">Christopher Hitchens</a>, among others who criticized Amnesty's association with Begg.
</p><p>After her suspension and the controversy, Sahgal was interviewed by numerous media and attracted international supporters. She was interviewed on the US <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" class="mw-redirect" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a> (NPR) on 27 February 2010, where she discussed the activities of Cageprisoners and why she deemed it inappropriate for Amnesty to associate with Begg.<sup id="cite_ref-npr_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> She said that Cageprisoners' Asim Qureshi spoke supporting global <i><a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">jihad</a></i> at a <a href="/wiki/Hizb_ut-Tahrir" title="Hizb ut-Tahrir">Hizb ut-Tahrir</a> rally.<sup id="cite_ref-npr_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> She stated that a bestseller at Begg's bookshop was a book by <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Azzam" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdullah Azzam">Abdullah Azzam</a>, a mentor of <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a> and a founder of the terrorist organization <a href="/wiki/Lashkar-e-Taiba" title="Lashkar-e-Taiba">Lashkar-e-Taiba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dd_139-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dd-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-npr_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a separate interview for the Indian <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_%26_Analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily News &amp; Analysis">Daily News &amp; Analysis</a></i>, Sahgal said that, as Quereshi affirmed Begg's support for global <i>jihad</i> on a<i> <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">BBC World Service</a></i> programme, "these things could have been stated in his [Begg's] introduction" with Amnesty.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> She said that Begg's bookshop had published <i>The Army of Madinah</i>, which she characterized as a <i>jihad</i> manual by <a href="/wiki/Dhiren_Barot" title="Dhiren Barot">Dhiren Barot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pay_controversy">Pay controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Pay controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2011, newspaper stories in the UK revealed that <a href="/wiki/Irene_Khan" title="Irene Khan">Irene Khan</a> had received a payment of £533,103 from Amnesty International following her resignation from the organization on 31 December 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-civsoc_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civsoc-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> a fact pointed to from Amnesty's records for the 2009–2010 financial year. The sum paid to her was more than four times her annual salary (£132,490).<sup id="cite_ref-civsoc_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civsoc-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The deputy secretary general, <a href="/wiki/Kate_Gilmore_(UN_official)" title="Kate Gilmore (UN official)">Kate Gilmore</a>, who also resigned in December 2009, received an ex-gratia payment of £320,000.<sup id="cite_ref-civsoc_144-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civsoc-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-expr_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expr-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Peter Pack, the chairman of Amnesty's International Executive Committee (IEC), initially stated on 19 February 2011: "The payments to outgoing secretary general Irene Khan shown in the accounts of AI (Amnesty International) Ltd for the year ending 31 March 2010 include payments made as part of a confidential agreement between AI Ltd and Irene Khan"<sup id="cite_ref-expr_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expr-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> and that "It is a term of this agreement that no further comment on it will be made by either party."<sup id="cite_ref-civsoc_144-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civsoc-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The payment and AI's initial response to its leakage to the press led to considerable outcry. <a href="/wiki/Philip_Davies" title="Philip Davies">Philip Davies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> MP for <a href="/wiki/Shipley_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Shipley (UK Parliament constituency)">Shipley</a>, criticized the payments, telling the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Express" title="Daily Express">Daily Express</a></i>: "I am sure people making donations to Amnesty, in the belief they are alleviating poverty, never dreamed they were subsidising a fat cat payout. This will disillusion many benefactors."<sup id="cite_ref-expr_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expr-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> On 21 February 2011, Peter Pack issued a further statement, in which he said that the payment was a "unique situation" that was "in the best interest of Amnesty's work" and that there would be no repetition of it.<sup id="cite_ref-civsoc_144-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civsoc-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> He stated that "the new secretary general, with the full support of the IEC, has initiated a process to review our employment policies and procedures to ensure that such a situation does not happen again."<sup id="cite_ref-civsoc_144-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civsoc-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Pack also stated that Amnesty was "fully committed to applying all the resources that we receive from our millions of supporters to the fight for human rights".<sup id="cite_ref-civsoc_144-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civsoc-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 February 2011, Pack sent a letter to Amnesty members and staff. In 2008, it stated, the IEC decided not to prolong Khan's contract for a third term. In the following months, IEC discovered that due to British employment law, it had to choose between three options: offering Khan a third term; discontinuing her post and, in their judgement, risking legal consequences; or signing a confidential agreement and issuing a pay compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2019_Report_on_workplace_bullying_within_Amnesty_International">2019 Report on workplace bullying within Amnesty International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 2019 Report on workplace bullying within Amnesty International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Amnesty_International#2019_Bullying_Report" title="Criticism of Amnesty International">Criticism of Amnesty International §&#160;2019 Bullying Report</a></div>
<p>In February 2019, Amnesty International's management team offered to resign after an independent report found what it called a "toxic culture" of <a href="/wiki/Workplace_bullying" title="Workplace bullying">workplace bullying</a>. Evidence of <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">bullying</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harassment" title="Harassment">harassment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">sexism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> was uncovered after two 2018 suicides were investigated: that of 30-year Amnesty veteran <a href="/wiki/Ga%C3%ABtan_Mootoo" title="Gaëtan Mootoo">Gaëtan Mootoo</a> in Paris in May 2018 (who left a <a href="/wiki/Suicide_note" title="Suicide note">note</a> citing work pressures); and that of 28-year-old intern Rosalind McGregor in Geneva in July 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-RTE2019-02-23a_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RTE2019-02-23a-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> An internal survey by the Konterra group with a team of psychologists was conducted in January 2019, after the 2 employees had killed themselves in 2018. The report stated that Amnesty had a toxic work culture and that workers frequently cited mental and physical health issues as a result of their work for the organization. The report found that: "39 per cent of Amnesty International staff reported that they developed mental or physical health issues as the direct result of working at Amnesty". The report concluded, "organisational culture and management failures are the root cause of most staff wellbeing issues.".<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Elaborating on this the report mentioned that bullying, public humiliation and other abuses of power are common place and routine practice by the management. It also claimed the us versus them culture among employees and the severe lack of trust in the senior management at Amnesty.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> By October 2019 five of the seven members of the senior leadership team at Amnesty's international secretariat left the organization with "generous" redundancy packages.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Among them, Anna Neistat, who was Gaëtan Mootoo's senior manager directly implicated in the independent report on Mootoo's death. According to Mootoo's former collaborator, Salvatore Saguès, "Gaëtan’s case is merely the tip of the iceberg at Amnesty. A huge amount of suffering is caused to employees. Since the days of Salil Shetty, when top management were being paid fabulous salaries, Amnesty has become a multinational where the staff are seen as dispensable. Human resources management is a disaster and nobody is prepared to stand up and be counted. The level of impunity granted to Amnesty’s bosses is simply unacceptable."<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> After none of the managers responsible of bullying at Amnesty were held accountable a group of workers petitioned for Amnesty's chief <a href="/wiki/Kumi_Naidoo" title="Kumi Naidoo">Kumi Naidoo</a> to resign. On 5 December 2019 Naidoo resigned from his post of Amnesty's Secretary General citing ill health<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> and appointing Julie Verhaar as an interim Secretary General. In their petition, workers demanded her immediate resignation as well.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kurdish_Hunger_Strike_occupation">Kurdish Hunger Strike occupation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Kurdish Hunger Strike occupation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2019, 30 <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish people">Kurdish</a> activists, some of whom are on an indefinite <a href="/wiki/Hunger_strike" title="Hunger strike">hunger strike</a>, occupied Amnesty International's building in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> in a peaceful protest, in order to speak out against Amnesty's silence on the isolation of <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_%C3%96calan" title="Abdullah Öcalan">Abdullah Öcalan</a> in a Turkish prison.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The hunger strikers have also spoken out about "delaying tactics" by Amnesty, and being denied access to toilets during the occupation, despite this being a human right.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Two of the hunger strikers, Nahide Zengin and Mehmet Sait Zengin, received <a href="/wiki/Paramedic" title="Paramedic">paramedic</a> treatment and were taken to hospital during the occupation. Late in the evening of 26 April 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police_Service" title="Metropolitan Police Service">London Met</a> police arrested 21 remaining occupiers.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2019_Budgetary_crisis_controversy">2019 Budgetary crisis controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 2019 Budgetary crisis controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2019 Amnesty International's Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Kumi_Naidoo" title="Kumi Naidoo">Kumi Naidoo</a> admitted to a hole in the organization's budget of up to £17m in donor money to the end of 2020. In order to deal with the budgetary crisis Naidoo announced to staff that the organization's headquarters would have cut almost 100 jobs as a part of urgent restructuring. <a href="/wiki/Unite_the_Union" title="Unite the Union">Unite the Union</a>, the UK's biggest trade union, said the redundancies were a direct result of "overspending by the organisation’s senior leadership team" and have occurred "despite an increase in income".<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Unite, which represents Amnesty's staff, feared that cuts would fall heaviest on lower income staff. It said that in the previous year the top 23 highest earners at Amnesty International were paid a total of £2.6m– an average of £113,000 per year. Unite demanded a review of whether it is necessary to have so many managers in the organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Amnesty's budgetary crisis became public after the two staff suicides in 2019. A subsequent independent review of workplace culture found a “state of emergency” at the organization after a restructuring process. Following several reports that labelled Amnesty a toxic workplace, in October 2019 five of the seven high-paid senior directors at Amnesty's international secretariat in London left the organization with "generous" redundancy packages<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>. This included Anna Neistat, who was a senior manager directly implicated in the independent report on the suicide of Amnesty's West Africa researcher Gaëtan Mootoo in the organization's Paris office. The size of exit packages granted to former senior management caused anger among other staff and an outcry among Amnesty's members.
</p><p>After the resignation of Amnesty International's Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Kumi_Naidoo" title="Kumi Naidoo">Kumi Naidoo</a> in December 2019, a new International Board was elected. In addition to leading the recovery period of the international secretariat, the Board also has to recruit a new Secretary General, manage costs, develop a new global strategy, and ensure delivery of Amnesty's activities. A new senior director, Chief Financial Officer Nigel Armitt, was appointed to the International Secretariat, to manage budgetary crisis. The company stated that Armitt "oversees financial management at the International Secretariat and is responsible for supporting and fostering the organisation’s financial literacy and capability"<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honours">Awards and honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Awards and honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1977, Amnesty International was awarded the Nobel Peace Prize for "having contributed to securing the ground for freedom, for justice, and thereby also for peace in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1984, Amnesty International received the Four Freedoms award in the category of Freedom of Speech.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1991, Amnesty International was awarded the journalistic prize <i>Golden Doves for Peace</i> by the "Archivio Disarmo" Research Center in Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_impact">Cultural impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cultural impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights_concerts">Human rights concerts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Human rights concerts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_concerts" title="Human rights concerts">Human rights concerts</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HumanRightsNowPhiladelphia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/HumanRightsNowPhiladelphia.jpg/225px-HumanRightsNowPhiladelphia.jpg" decoding="async" width="225" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/HumanRightsNowPhiladelphia.jpg/338px-HumanRightsNowPhiladelphia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/HumanRightsNowPhiladelphia.jpg/450px-HumanRightsNowPhiladelphia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1716" data-file-height="1139" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HumanRightsNowPhiladelphia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Opening stages of the 19 September 1988 show at <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/JFK_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="JFK Stadium">JFK Stadium</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/A_Conspiracy_of_Hope" title="A Conspiracy of Hope">A Conspiracy of Hope</a></i> was a short tour of six <a href="/wiki/Benefit_concert" title="Benefit concert">benefit concerts</a> on behalf of Amnesty International that took place in the United States during June 1986.  The purpose of the tour was not to raise funds but rather to increase awareness of human rights and of Amnesty's work on its 25th anniversary. The shows were headlined by <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams" title="Bryan Adams">Bryan Adams</a> and also featured <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gabriel" title="Peter Gabriel">Peter Gabriel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lou_Reed" title="Lou Reed">Lou Reed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Baez" title="Joan Baez">Joan Baez</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Neville_Brothers" title="The Neville Brothers">The Neville Brothers</a>. The last three shows featured a reunion of <a href="/wiki/The_Police" title="The Police">The Police</a>. At a press conferences in each city, at related media events, and through their music at the concerts themselves, the artists engaged with the public on themes of human rights and human dignity.  The six concerts were the first of what subsequently became known collectively as the Human Rights Concerts – a series of music events and tours staged by <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International_USA" title="Amnesty International USA">Amnesty International USA</a> between 1986–1998.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Now!" title="Human Rights Now!">Human Rights Now!</a></i> was a worldwide tour of twenty <a href="/wiki/Benefit_concert" title="Benefit concert">benefit concerts</a> on behalf of Amnesty International that took place over six weeks in 1988.  Held not to raise funds but to increase awareness of both the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> on its 40th anniversary and the work of Amnesty International, the shows featured <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen_and_the_E_Street_Band" class="mw-redirect" title="Bruce Springsteen and the E Street Band">Bruce Springsteen and the E Street Band</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gabriel" title="Peter Gabriel">Peter Gabriel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Chapman" title="Tracy Chapman">Tracy Chapman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Youssou_N%27Dour" title="Youssou N&#39;Dour">Youssou N'Dour</a>, plus guest artists from each of the countries where concerts were held.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artists_for_Amnesty">Artists for Amnesty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Artists for Amnesty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Amnesty International, through its "Artists for Amnesty" programme has also endorsed various cultural media works for what its leadership often consider accurate or educational treatments of real-world topics that fall within the range of Amnesty's concern:
</p>
<ul><li><i>A is for Auschwitz</i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/At_the_Death_House_Door" title="At the Death House Door">At the Death House Door</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Blood_Diamond_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood Diamond (film)">Blood Diamond</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Bordertown_(2006_film)" title="Bordertown (2006 film)">Bordertown</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Catch_a_Fire_(film)" title="Catch a Fire (film)">Catch a Fire</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/In_Prison_My_Whole_Life" title="In Prison My Whole Life">In Prison My Whole Life</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Invictus_(film)" title="Invictus (film)">Invictus</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Lord_of_War" title="Lord of War">Lord of War</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Rendition_(film)" title="Rendition (film)">Rendition</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Constant_Gardener_(film)" title="The Constant Gardener (film)">The Constant Gardener</a></i></li>
<li><i>Tibet: Beyond Fear</i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Trouble_the_Water" title="Trouble the Water">Trouble the Water</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/12_Years_a_Slave" class="mw-redirect" title="12 Years a Slave">12 Years a Slave</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Django_Unchained" title="Django Unchained">Django Unchained</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Help" title="The Help">The Help</a></i></li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amnesty_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-fn1-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-fn1_11-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn1_11-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The anthropologist Linda Rabben refers to the origin of Amnesty as a "creation myth" with a "kernel of truth": "The immediate impetus to form Amnesty did come from Peter Benenson's righteous indignation while reading a newspaper in the London tube on 19 November 1960."<sup id="cite_ref-Rabben_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rabben-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The historian Tom Buchanan traced the origins story to a radio broadcast by Peter Benenson in 1962. The 4 March 1962 BBC news story did not refer to a "toast to liberty", but Benenson said his tube ride was on 19 December 1960. Buchanan was unable to find the newspaper article about the Portuguese students in <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> for either month. Buchanan found many news stories reporting on the repressive Portuguese political arrests in <i>The Times</i> for November 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-Buchanan_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buchanan-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
